## Week 5.1 -- Other Suspect Classifications

### 1. **San Antonio I.S.D. v. RodrÃ­guez, 411 U.S. 1 (1973)**

> **Facts?**  
> â€“ Texas financed public schools through a statewide foundation program **plus** each districtâ€™s property-tax levy. Property-poor Edgewood I.S.D. raised far less per pupil than affluent Alamo Heights, even though Edgewood taxed itself at a ==_higher_== rate.

> **Plaintiffsâ€™ argument?**  
> â€“ The scheme discriminates against a **suspect class of poor children** and burdens the **fundamental right to education**, demanding strict scrutiny.

> **Stateâ€™s argument?**  
> â€“ Local control justifies relying on local property wealth; education is not a fundamental right and wealth is not a suspect class.

> **Issue?**  
> â€“ Does the Texas finance system violate the Equal Protection Clause because it creates wealth-based disparities in per-pupil spending?

> **Holding?**  
> â€“ **No.** Wealth is not a suspect classification and education, though important, is not a fundamental right; rational-basis review applies, and the system is rational.

> **Reasoning (Justice Powell):**  
> **First**, the plaintiffs could not define a discrete _indigent_ classâ€”poor families are scattered across districts.  
> **Second**, no child suffers an **absolute deprivation** of schooling; disparities are relative.  
> **Third**, strict scrutiny is reserved for suspect classes (race, alienage, etc.) or fundamental rights; neither is present.  
> **Fourth**, the system rationally furthers two legitimate goals: (1) **local fiscal autonomy** and (2) experimentation in educational policy.

> **Level of scrutiny?** â€“ **Rational-basis** (deferential).

> **Concurrence (Justice Stewart, solo)** 
> â€“ Agrees education is not a fundamental right and no suspect class is involved, so rational-basis review suffices; finds the Texas scheme satisfies that test.
    
> **Dissents**:
> **Justice White (joined by Douglas & Brennan)** 
> â€“ Local-wealth differentials _deprive poor districts of any real choice_ to raise funds; the scheme is irrational because equal tax effort yields radically unequal revenue. â€‹
> **Justice Marshall (joined by Douglas)** 
> â€“ Education is â€œvital to political and social lifeâ€ and should trigger heightened scrutiny; the State must show its means are substantially related to achieving legitimate goals, which it failed to do. â€‹

> **Significance:**  
> â€“ Rejected â€œpovertyâ€ as a suspect class; cemented the rule that most socioeconomic legislation gets minimal review and left school-finance reform to politics.

---

### 2. **Plyler v. Doe, 457 U.S. 202 (1982)**

> **Facts?**  
> â€“ Texas statute denied state funds and let local districts **exclude undocumented children** from free K-12 education.

> **Plaintiffsâ€™ argument?**  
> â€“ The law imposes a lifetime disability on children **not responsible** for their immigration status, violating equal protection.

> **Stateâ€™s argument?**  
> â€“ Texas may conserve resources for lawful residents and deter illegal immigration.

> **Issue?**  
> â€“ May a state bar undocumented school-age children from free public education?

> **Holding?**  
> â€“ **No.** Section 21.031 violates the Equal Protection Clause.

> **Reasoning (Justice Brennan):**  
> **First**, undocumented children are â€œ_persons_â€ within the Fourteenth Amendment.  
> **Second**, the classification is neither suspect nor wholly ordinary; education is not fundamental, **but** the deprivation is grave and permanent.  
> **Third**, Texasâ€™s asserted interests (saving money, discouraging migration, classroom burdens) are speculative and poorly tailored.  
> **Fourth**, the statute would create an illiterate underclass, harming the State and Nationâ€”so even under **â€œheightened rationalityâ€** the law fails.

> **Level of scrutiny?**
>  â€“ **â€œIntermediate-plusâ€ rational basis** (often called _rational basis with bite_).

> **Concurrence (Justice Marshall, solo)**:
> â€“ Reiterates his _RodrÃ­guez_ position: education _is_ a fundamental interest; the majority reaches the right result but should have applied strict scrutiny. â€‹ -- 

> **Dissent (Chief Justice Burger, joined by White, Rehnquist & Oâ€™Connor)**:
> â€“ The Court acts as â€œPlatonic Guardiansâ€; Texas may ration public resources and is not constitutionally compelled to educate those who entered unlawfully. â€‹

> **Significance:**  
> â€“ Shows the Court will stiffen rational-basis review when legislation targets a **vulnerable, innocent group** and jeopardizes core civic participation.

---

### 3. **City of Cleburne v. Cleburne Living Center, 473 U.S. 432 (1985)**

> **Facts?**  
> â€“ Cleburne required a special-use permit for a 13-person **group home for the mentally retarded**, yet allowed boarding houses, hospitals, dorms, etc., as of right in the same zone.

> **Plaintiffsâ€™ argument?**  
> â€“ The permit denial rested on irrational stereotypes and violated equal protection.

> **Cityâ€™s argument?**  
> â€“ Mentally retarded residents pose unique concerns (flood plain, junior-high harassment, density, legal liability).

> **Issue?**  
> â€“ Does denying the permit violate equal protection, and is **mental retardation** a quasi-suspect classification?

> **Holding?**  
> â€“ **Yes (as-applied)**; the ordinance is irrational here, but mental retardation is **not** a quasi-suspect class. **UNANIMOUS JUDGMENT.**

> **Reasoning (Justice White):** 
> **First**, heightened scrutiny is limited to groups with deep prejudice _and_ limited political power; recent legislation shows active political protection for the retarded.  
> **Second**, nonetheless the city offered **no rational link**: fears and neighbor hostility are illegitimate, flood risk applies equally to permitted uses, and size/density limits are inconsistently enforced.  
> **Third**, mere â€œbare desire to harm a politically unpopular groupâ€ is never legitimate.

> **Concurrences**:
> **Justice Stevens (joined by Burger & Powell)** 
> â€“ Would invalidate the permit requirement on traditional rational-basis grounds but stresses that insisting on a special permit â€œreflects only unthinking prejudice.â€
> **Justice Marshall (joined by Brennan & Blackmun) (concurring in part, dissenting in part)** 
> â€“ Agrees the ordinance is invalid but argues that _mental retardation deserves heightened scrutiny_ because of a long history of exclusion and the fundamental interest in establishing a home. â€‹

> **Level of scrutiny?** â€“ Formal **rational-basis**, but with searching inquiry (â€œrational-basis _with bite_â€). word games

> **Significance:**  
> â€“ Clarified that disability is **not** quasi-suspect, but also that irrational prejudice flunks even low-level review; became the template for later _animus_ cases.

### 4. **Romer v. Evans, 517 U.S. 620 (1996)**

> **Facts?**  
> â€“ Coloradoâ€™s **Amendment 2** barred state or local governments from enacting any law protecting persons from discrimination **on the basis of sexual orientation**.

> **Plaintiffsâ€™ argument?**  
> â€“ The amendment singles out gays and lesbians for a blanket disability and cannot survive even rational review.

> **Stateâ€™s argument?**  
> â€“ Amendment 2 prevents special preferences and upholds freedom of association.

> **Issue?**  
> â€“ Does Amendment 2 violate the Equal Protection Clause?

> **Holding?**  
> â€“ **Yes.** It fails even ordinary rational-basis review.

> **Reasoning (Justice Kennedy):**  
> **First**, equal protection requires a **connection** between a classification and a legitimate goal; here none exists.  
> **Second**, the amendment is _both too narrow and too broad_â€”it targets a single trait yet bans protection in every sphere.  
> **Third**, its breadth reveals a â€œ**bareâ€¦desire to harm**â€ an unpopular group, which is **not** a legitimate state interest (citing _Moreno_).  
> **Fourth**, by closing the political process to one class alone, Amendment 2 violates the core meaning of equal protection.

> **Level of scrutiny?** â€“ Nominal **rational-basis**, but explicitly animated by the _animus doctrine_.

> **Dissent (Justice Scalia, joined by Rehnquist & Thomas)**:
>  â€“ Faults the majority for inventing a new â€œanimusâ€ test; contends Amendment 2 is a permissible moral choice comparable to Bowers v. Hardwick, and that rational-basis review should uphold a law reflecting votersâ€™ moral disapproval of homosexuality. (Reasoning drawn from the opinion; no file excerpt available.)

> **Significance:**  
> â€“ First Supreme Court victory for LGBT rights; established that laws motivated by animus flunk equal protection without requiring heightened scrutiny, paving the way to _Lawrence_ and _Obergefell_.

### Quick Comparative Takeaway

| Case          | Suspect Class?            | Review Applied           | Courtâ€™s Core Logic (sound-bite)             |
| ------------- | ------------------------- | ------------------------ | ------------------------------------------- |
| **RodrÃ­guez** | None (wealth)             | Rational basis           | Local control justifies funding disparities |
| **Plyler**    | None (undocumented kids)  | â€œRational-plusâ€          | Penalizing innocent children is irrational  |
| **Cleburne**  | None (disability)         | Rational-basis-with-bite | Prejudice â‰  legitimate zoning rationale     |
| **Romer**     | None (sexual orientation) | Rational-basis-with-bite | Animus alone is not a public purpose        |

### Modern Equal Protection Classifications

- **Strict scrutiny (â â€œsuspect classâ€â )**  
    The State must show the law is _narrowly tailored_ to meet a _compelling_ interest. The Court has only put a few classifications here because history shows they trigger prejudice that politics canâ€™t easily cure.
- **Intermediate scrutiny (â â€œquasi-suspect classâ€â )**  
    The State must show the law is _substantially related_ to an _important_ interest. Sex (and illegitimacy) live here; the Court has _not_ formally moved sexual-orientation or gender-identity up from rational-basis, though the post-_Obergefell_ jurisprudence is functionally â€œrational-basis-plus.â€
- **Rational basis (ordinary or â€œwith biteâ€)**  
    Law must be _rationally related_ to a _legitimate_ interest. Age (_Murgia_), disability (_Cleburne_), wealth (_Rodriguez_), etc., stay here, but the Court occasionally uses a skeptical variant (â€œwith biteâ€) when it smells animus.

| **National Origin**                                                          | **Strict**                                              | _Hernandez v. Texas_ (1954); _Oyama_ (1948)                                                                                                      | Often travels with race; covers ancestry & ethnicity.                                                                                   |

Richardson_ (1971)                                                                                                                    | **Not** strict if (i) classification comes from **Congress** or (ii) is tied to â€œpolitical-community functionsâ€ (_Foley_ 1978).         |
| **Religion**                                                                 | **Strict** (as equal-protection classification)         | _Larson v. Valente_ (1982); _Lukumi_ (1993)                                                                                                      | Rare; most modern religious cases arise under the First Amendment, but the Court treats religious gerrymanders as suspect under EP too. |
| **Fundamental-right burdens** (voting, interstate travel, marriage, speechâ€¦) | **Strict** (even if the underlying group isnâ€™t suspect) | _Reynolds v. Sims_ (1964) (vote); _Saenz v. Roe_ (1999) (travel); _Obergefell_ (2015) (marriage)                                                 | Technically not a â€œclass,â€ but any line that burdens a fundamental right gets strict scrutiny.                                          |

| **Gender Identity**                                                          | No formal tier yet                                      | Cert. grants in 2024-25 (e.g., _Doe v. Oklahoma_) suggest forthcoming showdown, but current precedent applies _Romer_-style rational-basis-plus. |                                                                                                                                         |
| **Age**                                                                      | **Rational Basis**                                      | _Murgia_ (1976)                                                                                                                                  | Congressâ€”not the Courtâ€”elevated scrutiny legislatively (ADEA).                                                                          |
| **Disability**                                                               | **Rational-basis-plus**                                 | _City of Cleburne_ (1985)                                                                                                                        | ADA & Rehab Act now supply most bite; Court continues to apply deferential review.                                                      |
| **Poverty / Wealth**                                                         | **Rational Basis**                                      | _San Antonio v. Rodriguez_ (1973)                                                                                                                | Court has rejected a poverty suspect class.                                                                                             |

### Important Explicit/Implicit Positive Obligations

â€œPositive rightâ€ = an **affirmative governmental duty** (providing a good/service). Unlike European constitutions, ours is mostly negative-rights-oriented; but a handful of doctrines **DO** compel action:
- **Text-based, explicit** â€“ requirements baked into the instrument (jury, habeas, counsel, fair elections).
- **Doctrine-driven, implicit** â€“ obligations the Court inferred from Due Process, Equal Protection, or the Eighth Amendment (prison medical care, marriage licensing, etc.).

| Positive Duty the State Must Perform                                                  | Source (Clause + Lead Case)                                                                          | Scope & Limits (2025 snapshot)                                                                                           |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| **Provide counsel to indigent criminal defendants**                                   | 6th Am. & 14th Am.; _Gideon v. Wainwright_ (1963); _Argersinger_ (1972); _Alabama v. Shelton_ (2002) | Applies to any offense with actual imprisonment; extends to first appeal (_Douglas_ 1963).                               |
| **Furnish trial/appeal transcripts to indigent defendants**                           | 14th Am. DP & EP; _Griffin v. Illinois_ (1956)                                                       | Ensures _meaningful_ appeal accessâ€”not just paper availability.                                                          |
| **Conduct regular, equal, and fairly apportioned elections**                          | Art. I, Â§ 4; 14th Am. EP; _Baker v. Carr_ (1962); _Reynolds v. Sims_ (1964)                          | Requires states to draw districts of substantially equal population; triggers strict scrutiny for vote-dilution schemes. |
| **Issue marriage licenses on equal terms**                                            | Substantive DP & EP; _Loving v. Virginia_ (1967); _Obergefell v. Hodges_ (2015)                      | State must affirmatively provide access to the civil institution once it offers marriage at all.                         |
| **Maintain minimally adequate prison conditions & medical care**                      | 8th Am.; _Estelle v. Gamble_ (1976); _Brown v. Plata_ (2011)                                         | Duty is â€œdeliberate-indifferenceâ€ standard; can force states to spend money or release prisoners to comply.              |
| **Ensure basic access to elementary & secondary education for undocumented children** | 14th Am. EP; _Plyler v. Doe_ (1982)                                                                  | Limited to K-12 and only bars _exclusion_ or punitive tuition; does _not_ mandate equal funding.                         |
| **Habeas corpus availability**                                                        | Art. I, Â§ 9 (Suspension Cl.); _Boumediene v. Bush_ (2008)                                            | Federal courts must be open to test the lawfulness of detention unless Congress properly suspends.                       |
| **Provide library / legal-materials access for prisoners**                            | 1st & 14th Am. (access to courts); _Bounds v. Smith_ (1977); scaled back by _Lewis v. Casey_ (1996)  | Only to the extent necessary to file non-frivolous legal claims.                                                         |
| **Grand-jury indictment in federal felony cases**                                     | 5th Am.                                                                                              | Textual; does not bind the states (incorporation never happened).                                                        |

Issue: whether barring a subset of one gender is sufficient
Reason: Important government interest -- ok to reduce rate, all other remedies, equal arguments can be made that all young drivers since they overlap, and even worse it can be similar to the  that 90% of all are DUI, and then ban all alcohol, doesn't change the man or improve the education, the other consequences of infriging people's right to drive and make a living, so not narrowly tailored. The adequate and independent state ground doctrine states that when a litigant petitions the U.S. Supreme Court to review the judgment of a state court which rests upon both federal and non-federal (state) law, the U.S. Supreme Court does not have jurisdiction over the case if the state ground is (1) â€œadequateâ€ to support the judgment, and (2) â€œindependentâ€ of federal law.Â _SeeÂ [Michigan v. Long](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michigan_v._Long "Michigan v. Long")_, 463 U.S. 1032, 1038 (1983) (â€œIt is, of course, incumbent upon this Court to ascertain for itself whether the asserted non-federal ground independently and adequately supports the judgment.â€ (internal quotation marks omitted));Â _[Fox Film Corp. v. Muller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fox_Film_Corp._v._Muller "Fox Film Corp. v. Muller")_, 296 U.S. 207, 210 (1935) (â€œ[W]here the judgment of a state court rests upon two grounds, one of which is federal and the other non-federal in character, our jurisdiction fails if the non-federal ground is independent of the federal ground and adequate to support the judgment.â€);Â _[Murdock v. City of Memphis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murdock_v._City_of_Memphis "Murdock v. City of Memphis")_, ("[W]hether there exist other matters in the record actually decided by the State court which are sufficient to maintain the judgment of that court, notwithstanding the error in deciding the Federal question. In [that case] the court would not be justified in reversing the judgment of the State court.").

## Week 5.2 -- Affirmative Action

- Why it doesn't past rational basis review? Why is it not strict scrutiny.
- This term refers to groups that are distinct (discrete) and isolated (insular) from the mainstream political process.Â They are often characterized by an immutable or highly visible characteristic, such as race, that makes them easy to target for discrimination.Â 

1. Regents of the University of California v. Bakke, 438 U.S. 265 (1978)

> **Facts / Procedural Posture**  
> â€“ **UC-Davis Med School** set aside **16 of 100 seats** for applicants who identified as â€œBlacks, Chicanos, Asians, or American Indiansâ€ and who competed only against each other under a separate admissions track (â€œSpecial Admissionsâ€).  
> â€“ **Allan Bakke**, a 33-year-old white male engineer and former Marine with GPA = 3.46 & MCAT = 511/600, was rejected twice, while minority applicants with substantially lower scores were admitted under the set-aside.
> â€“ Bakke sued in **California superior court** â†’ won summary judgment â†’ **CA Supreme Court** struck the quota and ordered his admission. UC Regents sought cert.

> **Plaintiffâ€™s theory (Bakke)**  
> â€“ The quota is a **racial classification** triggering strict scrutiny under **Equal Protection (14A)** _and_ **Title VI** (because UC-Davis receives federal funds).  
> â€“ Remedies for societal discrimination are too amorphous; there is **no showing** that UC discriminated or that Bakke personally benefitted from past discrimination.

> **Universityâ€™s theory**  
> â€“ **Compelling interests**: (1) Remedying historic exclusion of minorities from medicine; (2) Improving medical care to underserved communities; (3) Training students for a diverse society; (4) Obtaining educational benefits of **classroom diversity** (Harvard-style rationale).  
> â€“ Quota is **narrowly tailored**: 16 seats (16%) â‰ˆ minority hospital-service population; race is **one factor** for the remaining 84 seats.

> **Issues**
> 1. Does the special-admissions quota violate the **Equal Protection Clause**?
> 2. Does it violate **Title VI of the Civil Rights Act (1964)**?
> 3. If unconstitutional, what is the proper remedy?

> **Holdings / Vote Map**  
> â€“ **No single majority opinion**; **Powellâ€™s opinion** (Parts I, III-C, IV, V) controls (4â€“1â€“4 alignment).
> - **Powell (1) + â€œliberal fourâ€ (Brennan, White, Marshall, Blackmun)** = 5 votes **to allow race as a _plus factor_**.
> - **Powell + â€œconservative fourâ€ (Burger, Rehnquist, Stewart, Stevens)** = 5 votes **to forbid a rigid quota & order Bakke admitted**.  
>     â€“ Result: **Quota invalid (Bakke admitted), but race-conscious holistic review permissible.**

> **Reasoning (Justice Powell, controlling)**  
> **Step 1 â€“ Standard of Review:**  
> â€“ Racial classifications by _any_ government actor are â€œ**inherently suspect**â€ â†’ **strict scrutiny** (same for benign vs. invidious).  
> **Step 2 â€“ Compelling Interest Analysis:**  
> â€“ **Remedying societal discrimination** = _too ill-defined_.  
> â€“ **Medical-service goals** & **countering shortage of minority doctors** = not shown.  
> â€“ **Classroom diversity** (Harvard plan) **is compelling** because it advances robust academic freedom.  
> **Step 3 â€“ Narrow Tailoring:**  
> â€“ A **fixed 16-seat quota** is _not narrowly tailored_: treats race as decisive, forecloses individual review, lacks flexibility, no logical sunset.  
> â€“ A **holistic system** that considers race as â€œone factor among manyâ€â€”e.g., Harvardâ€™s assigning an edge to â€œrace/ethnicityâ€ but pitting _all_ applicants in a single poolâ€”_would_ survive.  
> **Step 4 â€“ Statutory Mirror:**  
> â€“ **Title VI** is ==coextensive with Equal Protection== whenever the defendant is a state actor; same analysis, same result.

> **Concurrenceâ€“Dissent (Brennan, White, Marshall, Blackmun)**  
> â€“ **Standard of Review:** Only **intermediate scrutiny** for ==benign== racial classifications.  
> â€“ **Remedial & diversity interests** are compelling; the 16-seat set-aside is narrowly tailored.  
> â€“ Would **uphold the plan** in its entirety!

> **Concurrence (Stevens, joined by Burger, Rehnquist, Stewart)**  
> â€“ Focuses on **Title VI** text: race-based exclusion from a federally funded program is flatly prohibited; therefore, quota illegal **without** Equal-Protection analysis.  
> â€“ Would avoid constitutional question.

> **Level of Scrutiny Applied in Result:** **Strict scrutiny** (â€œsuspect classificationâ€); quota fails tailoring prong.

> **Significance / Aftermath**  
> â€“ First SCOTUS recognition that **diversity** can be a compelling state interest.  
> â€“ Provided the **Harvard holistic model** as a roadmap.  
> â€“ Spawned a trilogy: _Grutter v. Bollinger_ (2003) (upheld Michigan Lawâ€™s holistic use); _Gratz_ (2003) (struck undergrad point system); **ultimately overruled in part by _SFFA v. Harvard_ (2023)**, below.  
> â€“ Introduced the â€œ**Bakkeâ€two-step**â€: (1) diversity compelling, (2) quotas verboten.

> **Socratic-Class Landmines & Answers**  
> â€“ _Q:_ â€œDid Bakke create binding precedent if no majority?â€ 
> â†’ **Yes, under the Marks rule Powellâ€™s opinion controlling where five Justices concur in judgment on narrowest grounds.**  
> â€“ _Q:_ â€œIs Title VI broader than Equal Protection?â€ 
> â†’ **Not for state actors; but Title VI can reach private universities (e.g., Harvard) receiving federal funding; EP does not.**  
   â€“ _Q:_ â€œWhat tailoring tools did Powell suggest?â€ 
   â†’ **Individualized review, no fixed seat reservations, race as a â€˜tipâ€™ not a clincher, periodic end-point review.**

2. Students for Fair Admissions, Inc. v. President & Fellows of Harvard College, 600 U.S. â€” (2023) (consolidated with _SFFA v. UNC_)

> **Facts / Procedural Posture**  
> â€“ **Harvard (private, Title VI)** and **UNC (public, Equal Protection)** used holistic admissions where _self-identified_ race could boost a â€œpersonal rating.â€  
> â€“ **SFFA**, founded by activist Edward Blum, alleged discrimination against **Asian-American and white** applicants. District courts upheld both programs after lengthy bench trials; First Cir. affirmed Harvard judgment; Fourth Cir. interlocutory appeal pending for UNC. SCOTUS granted cert & heard both cases together.

> **Petitionerâ€™s theory (SFFA)**  
> â€“ **Strict scrutiny**: Diversity is **no longer compelling** (or never was), and even if it is, the plans are **not narrowly tailored** â†’ rely on racial stereotypes, lack end-point, and disadvantage Asians.  
> â€“ **Title VI** incorporates Equal Protection standards; Harvardâ€™s system thus unlawful.

> **Universitiesâ€™ theory**  
> â€“ Diversity remains compelling under **Bakke/Grutter** line; race is only **one contextual factor** among dozens; no quota or set-aside; periodic reviews show no workable race-neutral alternative.

> **Issues**
> 1. Should the Court **overrule _Bakke/Grutter_ and prohibit race-conscious admissions** altogether?
> 2. Even if those precedents stand, do Harvard & UNC fail strict scrutiny?

> **Holdings / Vote Map**  
> â€“ **6â€“3** (Roberts C.J.; Thomas, Alito, Gorsuch, Kavanaugh, Barrett):
> - **Race-based admissions violate the Equal Protection Clause & hence Title VI.**
> - **Bakke/Grutter â€œcannot be reconciledâ€ with core EP principle of color-blindness â†’ effectively overruled.**  
>     â€“ **Sotomayor diss. (joined by Kagan & Jackson for UNC part); Jackson diss. separately (recused from Harvard); both decry â€œhistorical amnesia.â€**

> **Majority Reasoning (Chief Justice Roberts)**  
> **Step 1 â€“ Strict Scrutiny Reaffirmed:**  
> â€“ Racial classifications are **â€œodiousâ€** and permissible only where _precisely_ tailored to a **truly compelling** interest.  
> **Step 2 â€“ Compelling Interest?**  
> â€“ Universitiesâ€™ asserted benefits (â€œtraining leaders,â€ â€œcombatting stereotypes,â€ â€œcivic engagementâ€) are **immeasurable, unreviewable, and lack a logical endpoint**.  
> â€“ Contrasts with _Brown_â€™s command that racial distinctions must be eliminated **â€œroot and branch.â€**  
> **Step 3 â€“ Narrow Tailoring?**  
> â€“ Data show **consistent racial balancing** (â€œstrikingly stableâ€ admit percentages).  
> â€“ **Race-neutral tools** (geographic, socioeconomic, first-gen preferences) were not seriously pursued.  
> â€“ Use of broad racial categories (**Asian, Hispanic, Black**) **masks intragroup diversity** and peddles stereotypes.
> **Step 4 â€“ Carve-outs & Caveats:**  
> â€“ **Military academies** get â€œno viewâ€â€”national-security briefs left open.  
> â€“ Applicants may still **describe how race affected them personally** (e.g., overcoming discrimination); but schools cannot **award a benefit â€œbecause of race itself.â€**

> **Thomas Concurrence**  
> â€“ History-textualism: Constitution **requires color-blindness**; raceâ€conscious remedies perpetuate stigma and harm intended beneficiaries.

> **Gorsuch Concurrence (joined by Thomas)**  
> â€“ **Title VI text** independently bars race-conscious admissions for _all_ federally funded schools, **public or private**.

> **Kavanaugh Concurrence**  
> â€“ Notes **25-year sunset** promised in _Grutter_ has arrived; racial preferences must end.

> **Sotomayor Dissent**  
> â€“ Calls majority â€œcolor-blind in theory, color-deaf in realityâ€; race still matters; diversity undeniably compelling; Court â€œcements a superficial rule of color-blindness.â€
> Brown is not about eliminating classification, but for equality. However, in reality, it's impossible to achieve equality without classification given the entrenched socio-economic, political disparities on the basis of race.

> **Jackson Dissent (UNC)**  
> â€“ Emphasizes **intergenerational racial inequality statistics**; warns of â€œlet-them-eat-cakeâ€ jurisprudence.

> **Level of Scrutiny Applied:** **Strict scrutiny** (and programs fail both prongs).

> **Significance / Immediate Fallout**  
> â€“ **Ends affirmative action** in virtually all higher-education admissions (except narrow potential pocket for service academies).  
> â€“ **Overrules the diversity rationale** as compellingâ€”though footnote allows race-linked _experiences_ discussion.  
> â€“ Revives debate on **legacy preferences**, socioeconomic factors, pipeline programs, and percentage-plan alternatives.  
> â€“ Expects **wave of litigation**: scholarships, faculty hiring, corporate DEI plans.

> **Socratic-Class Landmines & Answers**  
> â€“ _Q:_ â€œIs diversity _per se_ no longer compelling?â€ 
> â†’ **Majority: diversity goals â€œtoo amorphous.â€+ Even if compelling, tailoring fails. Effectively impossible to resurrect.**  
> â€“ _Q:_ â€œWhat about Title VI vs. EP after SFFA?â€ 
> â†’ **Gorsuch: Title VI textually bars any racial preferences in federally funded programsâ€”so private universities are doubly locked out.**  
> â€“ _Q:_ â€œWhy the military carve-out?â€ 
> â†’ **Majority cites unique national-security interests but takes no position; signals separate litigation ahead.**  
> â€“ _Q:_ â€œMay a Black applicant still write about racial adversity?â€ 
> â†’ **Yes, but admissions must evaluate that storyâ€™s _individual merit_, not award points because â€œBlack.â€**  
> â€“ _Q:_ â€œDoes SFFA expressly overrule _Bakke_?â€ 
> â†’ **Not in so many words, but by declaring its central premise (diversity as compelling interest) unworkable, the Court functionally discards it (â€œGrutter is abandoned, _Bakke_ reduced to historical artifactâ€).**

3. **Grutter v. Bollinger (2003)**

- **Facts**: White applicant denied admission to Michigan Law; challenged race-conscious admissions.
- **Issue**: Does holistic use of race in admissions violate Equal Protection?
- **Doctrines**: **Strict scrutiny**, **diversity as compelling interest**, **narrow tailoring**.
- **Holding**: **UPHELD** policy; diversity is compelling, and **individualized** review without quotas is narrowly tailored.

4. **Fisher v. UT Austin I (2013)**

- **Facts**: White applicant challenged UTâ€™s race-conscious admissions (top 10% plan + holistic review).
- **Issue**: Did lower courts apply the correct level of scrutiny?
- **Doctrines**: Clarified **strict scrutiny** must be **genuine, not deferential**.
- **Holding**: **REMANDED**; courts must rigorously test if race-neutral alternatives suffice.

5. **Fisher v. UT Austin II (2016)**

- **Facts**: Same case after remand; UT defended use of race as limited and justified.
- **Issue**: Does UTâ€™s policy survive **strict scrutiny**?
- **Doctrines**: **Strict scrutiny**, narrow tailoring, deference to **educational judgment**.
- **Holding**: **UPHELD** policy (4â€“3); race use was limited, periodic, and no workable race-neutral alternative existed.

3. **Regents of UC v. Bakke (1978)**

- **Facts**: White applicant denied by UC-Davis Med due to **16-seat racial quota**.
- **Issue**: Can race-based set-asides be used in admissions?
- **Doctrines**: **Strict scrutiny**, **Title VI**, **diversity rationale** (Powell).
- **Holding**: **Struck quota**, but **allowed race as one factor** in a holistic reviewâ€”**diversity = compelling**.

### **Quick Comparative Cheat-Sheet**

|Dimension|**Bakke (1978)**|**SFFA (2023)**|
|---|---|---|
|**Classification Level**|Strict scrutiny (suspect class)|Strict scrutiny reaffirmed|
|**Compelling Interest Recognized**|_Powell_: â€œDiversityâ€ in education|Majority: Diversity **not** compelling (too abstract)|
|**Tailoring Test**|No quotas; individualized â€œplus factorâ€ OK|Any race â€œtipâ€ invalid; only _race-linked experience_ narrative may be weighed|
|**Outcome**|Quota struck; holistic race consideration survives|Harvard/UNC plans struck; general race consideration barred|
|**Key Legacy**|Launched 45 yrs of permissible affirmative action|Shuts the door on affirmative action; raises Title VI color-blind bar|

## Additional Affirmative Action Notes 

### On SFFA v. Harvard/UNC

- Grutter v. Bollinger
	- Compelling interest for a diverse student body
	- do not use quotas or racial balancing are narrowly tailored when there are no effective race neutral alternatives available
- Fisher I 2013
- Fisher II 2016
- Bakke 1978

**Edward Blum** is a conservative legal strategist and the founder/president of **Students for Fair Admissions (SFFA)**.
- Heâ€™s not a lawyer but has **engineered several landmark Supreme Court cases** (e.g., _Shelby County v. Holder_ on the Voting Rights Act).
- His mission is to **eliminate racial classifications** in education, voting, and employment.
- His critics argue heâ€™s promoting a **colorblind legal ideology** that ignores structural inequity; his supporters view him as defending **individual merit and legal neutrality**.

> **What the fuck is he thinking?**  
> Blum believes the Constitution requires a **race-neutral society**, where race **should not be used** by public institutions **at all**, even to remedy past or current discrimination. He sees affirmative action as a form of **reverse discrimination**.

### âœ³ï¸ Reaffirmed 4 Key Limits on Race-Conscious Programs:

1. **No use of race as a _negative_:** A program cannot disadvantage individuals based on their race (e.g., Asian Americans).
2. **No reinforcement of _stereotypes_:** Race must not be used in a way that assumes anything about a personâ€™s traits or abilities.
3. **Must be _measurably connected_ to goals:** Abstract invocations of â€œdiversityâ€ are not enoughâ€”there must be **clear metrics** and endpoints.
4. **Race-conscious programs must have a _logical endpoint_:** Permanent race-based policies are unconstitutional. Diversity cannot be so vague that schools never know when theyâ€™ve achieved it.

Despite public confusion, the ruling **does not ban** all attempts to increase diversity:

| Permissible Strategies                        | Examples                                                                                                                                    |
| --------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Race-neutral programs**                     | % plans (e.g., top 10% of each high school), SES-based admissions, adversity scoring, first-gen preference                                  |
| **Holistic review of racialized experiences** | Applicants _may still write about_ how race shaped their identity, struggle, or valuesâ€”**but race itself cannot be the determining factor** |
| **Increased need-based aid**                  | More financial aid for low-income applicants                                                                                                |
| **Redefining â€œmeritâ€**                        | Moving beyond test scores to include community service, leadership, overcoming hardship                                                     |
| **Removing structural barriers**              | Dropping standardized tests, legacy preferences, app fees                                                                                   |
| **Campus DEIA programs**                      | Support for affinity groups, anti-discrimination systems, diverse faculty hiring                                                            |

### âŒ Is this truly about _merit_?

Many critics argue the decision **undermines holistic admissions** by ignoring how race intersects with:
- Wealth & poverty
- Generational disadvantage
- Neighborhood & school segregation
- Trauma and resilience

Some scholars argue this returns admissions to a **false â€œneutralâ€ standard**â€”one that historically benefited wealthy, white, and legacy students.

> Is â€œcolorblindnessâ€ just?  
> Is it _justice as formal equality_ (treating everyone the same), or _justice as substantive equality_ (giving people what they need to thrive)?

> ...to the point where we see that race is a fact, but not the defining fact and not the fact that tells us what is important, but we are not there yet. Until we are, race-conscious admissions programs that survive strict scrutiny will have an important place in society and help ensure that colleges and universities can offer a diverse atmosphere that fosters learning, improves scholarship, and encourages mutual respect and understanding. 
> -- District Court Judge Allison Burrough

## Week 6.1 -- Free Speech

### Categoriesâ€¯ofâ€¯Speech

- **Unprotectedâ€¯Speech** _(rationalâ€‘basis review, unless selective enforcement triggers scrutiny)_
    - Incitement to **imminent** lawless action (_Brandenburg_)
    - â€œFighting wordsâ€ likely to provoke retaliatory violence (_Chaplinsky_)
    - **True threats**â€”serious expression of intent to harm (_Virginiaâ€¯v.â€¯Black; Counterman_)
    - Obscenity failing the _Miller_ threeâ€‘part test
- **Lessâ€‘Protectedâ€¯Speech**
    - Sexually oriented but nonâ€‘obscene expression (_Renton_; _Erznoznik_)
    - Profane/indecent speech (FCC broadcast carveâ€‘outs; _Pacificâ€¯a_)
    - Commercial speechâ€”truthful but regulable under _Centralâ€¯Hudson_
- **Fullyâ€¯Protectedâ€¯Speech**
    - All remaining content, including hate speech, political advocacy, artistic expressionâ€”government must satisfy **strict scrutiny**
    - Courtâ€™s historic bias _in favorem_ libertatis except in â€œhistoric and traditionalâ€ exceptions

### Threeâ€¯Approachesâ€¯toâ€¯theâ€¯Firstâ€¯Amendment

- **Absolutist** â€“ â€œno law means NO LAWâ€ (Justice Blackâ€™s view)
- **Categorical** â€“ slot speech into protected/unprotected boxes; if unprotected, rational basis (_Chaplinsky_ framework)
- **Balancing** â€“ caseâ€‘byâ€‘case weighing of speakerâ€™s interest vs. governmental interest (Handâ€™s _Dennis_ formula; modern intermediate scrutiny)

### Typesâ€¯ofâ€¯RestrictionsÂ (con Examples)

- **Contentâ€‘Neutral (Time/Place/Manner)**
    - Ban on picketing private homes (_Frisby_)
    - Prohibition of any signs on utility poles
    - Nightâ€‘time amplifiedâ€‘sound curfew
    - Permit required for >50 persons in a park
- **Subjectâ€‘Matter Based**
    - Ban on **all** warâ€‘themed demonstrationsâ€”pro or anti
    - Home picketing allowed **only** for labor disputes
    - Judicial candidates barred from discussing â€œdisputed legal or political issuesâ€ (_Williamsâ€‘Yulee_)
- **Viewpoint Based**
    - Ban on **antiâ€‘war** protests (but proâ€‘war allowed)
    - Ban on signs **critical** of foreign governments near embassies
    - TikTok executiveâ€‘order targeting â€œChineseâ€‘owned speech platformâ€ could be argued viewpointâ€‘discriminatory under _R.A.V._

### Levelsâ€¯ofâ€¯Judicialâ€¯Scrutiny

- **Rationalâ€¯Basis** â€“ contentâ€‘neutral limits on unprotected speech
- **Intermediateâ€¯Scrutiny** â€“ contentâ€‘neutral limits on protected speech (_Oâ€™Brien_ symbolicâ€‘burning test)
- **Strictâ€¯Scrutiny** â€“ any contentâ€‘based (subjectâ€‘matter or viewpoint) restriction on **any** speech

### Twoâ€¯Modesâ€¯ofâ€¯Challenge

- **â€œAsâ€‘Appliedâ€ Challenge**
    - Tests whether _my_ conviction punishes protected speech
    - E.g., Nationalâ€‘security secrets law applied to auntâ€™s cookie recipe
    - **Chillingâ€‘effect** argument: selfâ€‘censorship through vagueness or overbreadth in individual case
- **Facial Challenge**
    - Argues statute is invalid in all (or substantial) applications
    - Tools: **Voidâ€‘forâ€‘Vagueness** & **Substantialâ€¯Overbreadth**
    - Good practice: plead **both** claims whenever viable

### Judicialâ€¯ReviewÂ Matrix

- Must track **(1) category of speech**, **(2) type of restriction**, **(3) posture (facialâ€¯vsâ€¯asâ€‘applied)**
- Contentâ€‘based on protected speech â†’ strict scrutiny (rarely survives)
- Contentâ€‘neutral on protected speech â†’ intermediate scrutiny (must be narrow, alternative channels)
- Viewpointâ€‘based on even unprotected speech â†’ invalid per _R.A.V._

### Proceduralâ€¯Dueâ€¯Process â€“ Voidâ€¯forâ€¯Vagueness

- â€œMen of common intelligence must not guessâ€ (_Connally_, 1926)
- Statute must define offense so ordinary people understand & does not encourage arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement (_Kolender_, 1983)

### Publicâ€‘Forumâ€¯Doctrineâ€¯(+â€¯Examples)

- **Traditional Public Forum** â€“ streets, sidewalks, parks (Grantâ€¯Park, Chicago)
- **Designated Public Forum (Unlimited)** â€“ cityâ€‘owned theatre opened for any event, university freeâ€‘speech zones (UCLA â€œBruinâ€¯Walkâ€ when booked)
- **Designated Public Forum (Limited/Purposeâ€‘Bound)** â€“ school board meeting for curriculum comments, Northwestern lecture hall reserved for academic debate
- **Nonpublic Forum** â€“ airport terminals (_ISKCON_), courthouse interiors, publicâ€‘school classrooms during instructional hours
- **Private Property** â€“ shopping malls (under _Pruneyard_ only in some states), Northwestern dorms; governed primarily by trespass law

### Rapidâ€‘Reference â€“ Content (Actual Speech)â€¯vsâ€¯Context (Online Platform) Restriction

- **TikTok ban**: arguably contentâ€‘neutral nationalâ€‘security regulation (_context_), but critics allege discriminatory treatment of Chineseâ€‘owned speech platform (_content/viewpoint_)
- **Flagâ€‘burning** (_Texasâ€¯v.â€¯Johnson_): contextâ€‘based (fire safety) struck down because law targeted **one symbolic message** â†’ contentâ€‘based

### 1. _Smith v_.Â _Goguen_, 415 U.S. 566 (1974)

> **Factsâ€¯/â€¯Proceduralâ€¯Posture**  
> â€“â€¯**Massachusetts G.â€¯L. c.â€¯264â€¯Â§â€¯5** made it a crime publicly to â€œtreat contemptuouslyâ€ the U.S. flag.  
> â€“â€¯**Joseph Goguen**, 18â€‘yearâ€‘old antiâ€‘war protester, was arrested in Worcester for wearing a small cloth flag sewn to the seat of his jeans. A state jury (after instructions that â€œcontemptuousâ€ meant whatever _they_ thought showed disrespect) convicted him; sentence of one year (suspended).  
> â€“â€¯Massachusetts Supreme Judicial Court affirmed. Goguen then won federal habeas relief in District Court; Firstâ€¯Circuit reversed, reinstating the conviction. **SCOTUS granted certiorari.**

> **Petitionerâ€™s Theory (Commonwealth of Massachusetts)**  
> â€“â€¯Flag protection statute is **narrow, intelligible, and longâ€‘standing**; ordinary citizens understand what â€œcontemptuousâ€ flag treatment means.  
> â€“â€¯Law regulates **conduct, not expression**; any expressive elements are incidental and outweighed by state interest in preserving a national symbol.  
> â€“â€¯Even if Firstâ€‘Amendment interests are implicated, the statute is comparable to regulations on draftâ€‘card destruction (_Oâ€™Brien_) and survives **intermediate scrutiny**.

> **Respondentâ€™s Theory (Goguen)**  
> â€“â€¯Statute is **unconstitutionally vague** under the **Due Process Clause**: gives no objective standard, invites adâ€‘hoc, **contentâ€‘based enforcement** against unpopular speakers.  
> â€“â€¯By empowering police/juries to punish â€œdisrespect,â€ the law **chills core political speech** and discriminates against dissenters.  
> â€“â€¯Unlike _Oâ€™Brien_, the stateâ€™s interest is **viewpointâ€‘driven respect**, not a neutral administrative goal; thus fails any Firstâ€‘Amendment balancing.

> **Issues**
> 1. Does Â§â€¯5 violate **Fourteenthâ€‘Amendment Due Process** because â€œtreats contemptuouslyâ€ is impermissibly **vague**?
> 2. If *not* void for vagueness, does it nonetheless abridge **free expression** protected by the First Amendment?

> **Holdingsâ€¯/â€¯Vote Map**  
> â€“â€¯**6â€“3** _(Powell, J.)_: Â§â€¯5 is **void for vagueness**; conviction reversed.  
> â€“â€¯**Burgerâ€¯C.J., Rehnquist, White** dissent.  
> â€“â€¯(No need to reach broader Firstâ€‘Amendment question once vagueness determined.)

> **Majority Reasoning (Justiceâ€¯Powell)**  
> **Stepâ€¯1 â€“ Vagueness Doctrine:**  
> â€“â€¯Criminal statutes must furnish **â€œexplicit standardsâ€** to give fair notice and prevent arbitrary enforcement (_Connally_; _Papachristou_).  
> **Stepâ€¯2 â€“ Application to Â§â€¯5:**  
> â€“â€¯Key term â€œcontemptuouslyâ€ â€œ_fails to draw reasonably clear lines between lawful and unlawful conduct_.â€  
> â€“â€¯Statute **delegates resolution of fundamental policy** (â€œwhat counts as disrespectâ€) to **police, prosecutors, and juries on an adâ€‘hoc basis**, creating a risk of **viewpoint discrimination**.  
> **Stepâ€¯3 â€“ Distinguishing Precedent:**  
> â€“â€¯Unlike narrowly drawn flagâ€‘desecration bans on **physical destruction** (_Street_) or **governmentâ€‘owned flags** (_Spence_), Â§â€¯5 sweeps in any behavior a particular jury dislikes.  
> â€“â€¯Massachusetts cannot salvage the law by **â€œjudicial narrowingâ€**; text is inherently standardâ€‘less.  
> **Result:** Conviction set aside; statute unconstitutional _as applied_, and effectively **facially void**.

> **Concurrence (Justiceâ€¯Douglas)**  
> â€“â€¯Would reach the **First Amendment** and hold that punishing symbolic expressionâ€”no matter how definedâ€”violates **core political speech principles** announced in _Stromberg_ and _Barnette_.  
> â€“â€¯Warns that deferential â€œrespectâ€‘forâ€‘flagâ€ statutes inevitably become tools against unpopular dissent.

> **Dissent (Justiceâ€¯Rehnquist, joined by Burgerâ€¯C.J. & White)**  
> â€“â€¯States may legitimately protect a unifying national emblem; â€œcontemptuousâ€ has a **plain meaning** understood by average citizens, parallel to â€œobsceneâ€ in _Miller_.  
> â€“â€¯Court improperly stretches vagueness to strike a law merely because it dislikes the policy; majority should defer to state definitions and _Oâ€™Brien_ balancing.

> **Level of Scrutiny Applied**  
> â€“â€¯**Vagueness / Dueâ€‘Process analysis**, not classic strictâ€‘vsâ€‘intermediate tiers; focus on **fairâ€‘notice & antiâ€‘arbitrariness**.  
> â€“â€¯Firstâ€‘Amendment merits expressly left unresolved (majority), though concurrence would apply **strict scrutiny** to speech regulation.

> **Significanceâ€¯/â€¯Immediate Fallout**  
> â€“â€¯Reaffirmed that **symbolicâ€‘speech statutes must give clear, objective standards**, laying groundwork for later flagâ€‘burning victories (_Spence_â€¯â€™74, _Johnson_â€¯â€™89).  
> â€“â€¯Illustrates Courtâ€™s **twoâ€‘track flag cases**: vagueness (due process) v. viewpoint (First Amendment).  
> â€“â€¯Signaled that mere legislative appeals to patriotic unity will not excuse **standardâ€‘less criminal bans**.  
> â€“â€¯Invited legislatures to rewrite flagâ€‘protection laws with **narrow, conductâ€‘specific language**â€”many states attempted â€œuniform codeâ€ amendments postâ€‘1974.

> **Socraticâ€‘Class Landminesâ€¯&â€¯Answers**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œIf â€˜contemptuousâ€™ is vague, why isnâ€™t â€˜obsceneâ€™ in _Miller_ equally vague?â€  
> â†’ **Miller supplied a **threeâ€‘part test**; Â§â€¯5 had no comparable objective elements.**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œCould Massachusetts salvage the law by defining misconduct more precisely (e.g., burning, defacing)?â€  
> â†’ **Yesâ€”the Court hints that a **specificâ€‘acts statute** might survive vagueness (though still faces Firstâ€‘Amendment attack).**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œDoes the ruling mean _all_ flagâ€‘respect laws are void?â€  
> â†’ **Noâ€”only those lacking clear, objective standards; physicalâ€‘destruction bans tied to fire safety or property interests may pass muster.**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œWhy not decide the Firstâ€‘Amendment question directly?â€  
> â†’ **Powell prefers the **narrowestâ€‘grounds rule**; once vagueness suffices, no need to reach broader speech issues.**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œHow does Goguen fit into the later _Texasâ€¯v.â€¯Johnson_ narrative?â€  
> â†’ **Goguen softens the ground: it strips away vague â€˜disrespectâ€™ statutes, forcing states into narrower bans that _Johnson_ will later strike on **contentâ€‘based grounds**.**

### 2. *Airport Comm'rs v. Jews for Jesus*, 482 U.S. 569 (1987)

> **Factsâ€¯/â€¯Proceduralâ€¯Posture**  
> â€“â€¯In **1983** the **Losâ€¯Angeles Board of Airport Commissioners** adopted **ResolutionÂ No.â€¯13787** declaring that the entire **Central Terminal Area (CTA) of LAX â€œis not open for Firstâ€¯Amendment activitiesâ€** and directing the City Attorney to sue anyone engaged in such conduct.
> â€“â€¯On **Julyâ€¯6â€¯1984** **Alan â€œAviâ€â€¯Snyder**, a minister with **Jewsâ€¯forâ€¯Jesus,â€¯Inc.**, was stopped while handing out free religious leaflets on an outdoor pedestrian ramp; an airport officer showed him the resolution and ordered him off the premises.
> â€“â€¯Snyder and Jewsâ€¯forâ€¯Jesus sued in the **C.D.â€¯California** for declaratory and injunctive relief, alleging the rule was facially unconstitutional, vague, and discriminatorily enforced. The district court (on stipulated facts) held the CTA a public forum and struck the rule; the **Ninth Circuit affirmed**. SCOTUS granted cert.

> **Petitionerâ€™s Theory (Board of Airport Commissioners)**  
> â€“â€¯**Airportâ€‘security & trafficâ€‘flow** justify a **total ban**; LAX terminals are, at most, a **nonpublic forum**, so regulations need only be **reasonable and viewpointâ€‘neutral**.  
> â€“â€¯Overbreadth doctrine does not apply because the Board intended the rule to cover only **nonâ€‘airportâ€‘related expressive activity** that could impede operations.

> **Respondentsâ€™ Theory (Jewsâ€¯forâ€¯Jesus & Snyder)**  
> â€“â€¯Resolution is **facially overbroad**: it criminalizes even silent prayer, wearing a political button, or casual conversation; no narrowing construction possible.  
> â€“â€¯Even in a nonpublic forum an **absolute speech ban** is unreasonable and violates the First Amendment; the rule also invites **selective enforcement**.

> **Issues**
> 1. Does ResolutionÂ 13787 violate the **First Amendment** by banning all â€œFirstâ€¯Amendment activitiesâ€ inside LAXâ€™s central terminal?
> 2. Must the Court decide whether an airport terminal is a **public forum** before resolving the challenge?

> **Holdingsâ€¯/â€¯Vote Map**  
> â€“â€¯**9â€¯â€“â€¯0** (Opinion: **Oâ€™Connor,â€¯J.**)â€¯â†’â€¯**Resolution facially violates the First Amendment under the overbreadth doctrine**; judgment of Ninth Circuit affirmed.  
> â€“â€¯**White,â€¯J. (joined by Rehnquist,â€¯C.J.) concurring**: agrees on overbreadth, but would emphasize that airports are not traditional public fora.

> **Majority Reasoning (Justiceâ€¯Oâ€™Connor)**  
> **Stepâ€¯1Â â€“Â Overbreadth Framework**  
> â€“â€¯A law is invalid if its **â€œplain languageâ€** prohibits **a substantial amount of protected speech** relative to its legitimate sweep (_Broadrick_, _Ferber_).  
> **Stepâ€¯2Â â€“Â Application to Resolution 13787**  
> â€“â€¯Text bars **â€œall Firstâ€¯Amendment activitiesâ€**: encompasses political discussion, reading a newspaper, humming a hymnâ€”speech that could not conceivably endanger airport safety.  
> â€“â€¯Such a sweeping ban would be unconstitutional **even in a nonpublic forum** because **no governmental interest** justifies eliminating _all_ expression.  
> **Stepâ€¯3Â â€“Â No Saving Construction**  
> â€“â€¯Boardâ€™s invitation to infer a â€œspeechâ€‘unrelatedâ€‘toâ€‘airportâ€‘purposesâ€ gloss is too **vague** and **delegates unfettered discretion** to airport police; Court declines to rewrite the ordinance.  
> **Stepâ€¯4Â â€“Â Forum Status Unnecessary**  
> â€“â€¯Because the regulation is **patently overbroad**, the Court need **not decide** whether LAXâ€™s CTA is a traditional, designated, or nonpublic forum.

> **White Concurrence (joined by Rehnquistâ€¯C.J.)**  
> â€“â€¯Airports are typically **nonpublic fora**; the Board could enact **reasonable, contentâ€‘neutral timeâ€‘placeâ€‘manner limits** focused on congestionâ€”but a total ban overshoots.

> **Level of Scrutiny Applied**  
> â€“â€¯**Facial overbreadth / reasonableness test**: even the minimal standard for nonpublic fora condemns an **absolute, contentâ€‘neutral but total** prohibition on speech.

> **Significanceâ€¯/â€¯Immediate Fallout**  
> â€“â€¯Landmark reminder that **government may not adopt a blanket speech embargo** on its property, no matter the forum classification.  
> â€“â€¯Invigorated the **overbreadth doctrine** as a swift tool to strike facial bans, forcing governments to craft **narrow, objective rules** (e.g., designated leafleting zones, permit systems).  
> â€“â€¯Influenced later airportâ€‘speech cases and analogous disputes in transit hubs, shopping malls, and train stations; many authorities rewrote rules to target **specific disruptions** rather than expression per se.

> **Socraticâ€‘Class Landminesâ€¯&â€¯Answers**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œIf the Court didnâ€™t decide whether an airport is a public forum, what guidance remains?â€  
> â†’ **Any forum test still forbids an _absolute_ ban; agencies must tailor regulations to concrete harms like obstruction or security, not to speech itself.**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œCould LAX limit leafleting to kiosks or curbside areas?â€  
> â†’ **Probably yesâ€”if the rule is **contentâ€‘neutral, leaves ample alternatives, and is tied to congestion or security evidence.**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œDoes this case make airports â€˜freeâ€‘speech zonesâ€™?â€  
> â†’ **No. It only invalidates a _total_ prohibition; reasonable, narrowly tailored restrictions remain permissible.**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œWhy is overbreadth different from vagueness?â€  
> â†’ **Overbreadth protects _thirdâ€‘party speakers_ by striking a statute that sweeps too widely; vagueness targets lack of clear standards.**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œWould a ban on â€˜distribution of literature that interferes with passenger flowâ€™ survive?â€  
> â†’ **Maybeâ€”Court would demand evidence that leafleting _actually_ disrupts operations and that the ban is no broader than necessary.**

### 3. *Keyishian v. Board of Regents*, 385 U.S. 589 (1967)

> **Factsâ€¯/â€¯Proceduralâ€¯Posture**  
> â€“â€¯Newâ€¯Yorkâ€™s **Civil Service Law Â§â€¯105** and **Education Law Â§â€¯3022 (the â€œFeinberg Lawâ€)** required every teacher or professor employed by the State University of Newâ€¯York to sign a **â€œloyalty certificateâ€** disavowing Communistâ€‘party membership and to affirm they had never advocated â€œthe overthrow of the government by force or violence.â€  
> â€“â€¯The Regents could list â€œsubversive organizationsâ€; **mere knowing membership**â€”even without active advocacyâ€”was grounds for dismissal.  
> â€“â€¯**Harry Keyishian** (English instructor) and four SUNYâ€‘Buffalo colleagues refused to sign; they were fired and sued for declaratory and injunctive relief in the **W.D.â€¯Newâ€¯York**. District court upheld the statutes; the **Secondâ€¯Circuit affirmed** (2â€‘1). SCOTUS granted certiorari and heard argument Octoberâ€¯17â€‘18â€¯1966.

> **Stateâ€™s Theory (Board of Regents & Attorney General)**  
> â€“â€¯The State has a **compelling interest** in preserving an educational workforce loyal to constitutional government; Â§â€¯105 targets **action, not opinion**.  
> â€“â€¯Statutes are patterned on **clear federal precedents** (e.g., _Cleveland Board of Education v. LaFleur_?) (They actually relied on _Adler v. Board of Education_, 1952) and provide adequate procedural safeguards: notice, opportunity to resign, review by Commissioner of Education.  
> â€“â€¯Academic employment is a **privilege, not a right**; the State may attach reasonable conditions (no subversive activity) to that privilege.

> **Petitionersâ€™ Theory (Keyishian etâ€¯al.)**  
> â€“â€¯Laws are **overbroad and vague**: terms like â€œtreasonable,â€ â€œseditious,â€ â€œadvocacyâ€ lack objective content and chill legitimate debate.  
> â€“â€¯Punishing **mere membership** in a proscribed groupâ€”without proof of specific intentâ€”conflicts with _Noto_, _Scales_, _Elfbrandt_.  
> â€“â€¯Statutes impose an **ideological orthodoxy** on public universities, violating the **First Amendmentâ€™s core protection of academic freedom**.

> **Issues**
> 1. Do Newâ€¯Yorkâ€™s loyaltyâ€‘certificate and subversiveâ€‘membership provisions violate the **First and Fourteenth Amendments** as **vague, overbroad, and a prior restraint on academic freedom**?
> 2. Should **_Adler v. Board of Education_ (1952)**â€”which upheld a predecessor loyalty lawâ€”be overruled?

> **Holdingsâ€¯/â€¯Vote Map**  
> â€“â€¯**5â€¯â€“â€¯4** (Opinion: **Brennan,â€¯J.**; joined by Warrenâ€¯C.J., Douglas, Fortas, Black) â€¯â†’â€¯**Statutes are unconstitutionally vague & overbroad; convictions reversed; _Adler_ effectively overruled.**  
> â€“â€¯**Clark, Harlan, Stewart, White** dissented (Clark opinion).

> **Majority Reasoning (Justiceâ€¯Brennan)**  
> **Stepâ€¯1 â€“ Overbreadth & Vagueness**  
> â€“â€¯Statutes reach â€œ_advocacy in the abstract_â€ and impose liability for **passive organizational membership**â€”a direct clash with _Noto_ and _Elfbrandt_.  
> â€“â€¯Key terms (â€œtreasonable,â€ â€œseditious,â€ â€œutter before any classâ€) provide **no objective standards**, leaving teachers to guess at what speech risks dismissalâ€”classic _Baggett_ vagueness.  
> **Stepâ€¯2 â€“ Academic Freedom as a Firstâ€‘Amendment â€œSpecial Concernâ€**  
> â€“â€¯â€œ_The classroom is peculiarly the marketplace of ideas._â€ Government may not cast a â€œpall of orthodoxyâ€ over universities; rigorous scrutiny applies.  
> **Stepâ€¯3 â€“ Overruling _Adler_**  
> â€“â€¯Experience since 1952 shows loyalty schemes **chill debate far beyond any legitimate security aim**; _Adler_â€™s reasoning incompatible with modern Firstâ€‘Amendment doctrine.  
> **Result:** Statutes facially invalid; reinstatement and backâ€‘pay relief left to lower courts.

> **Concurrence (Justiceâ€¯Douglas)**  
> â€“â€¯Stresses that any **ideological blacklist** in public employment offends the First Amendment, regardless of vagueness. Academic freedom demands an **absolute bar** to such loyalty requirements.

> **Dissent (Justiceâ€¯Clark, joined by Harlan, Stewart, White)**  
> â€“â€¯States may demand **â€œorthodox loyaltyâ€ to constitutional processes** from public servants; the Feinberg Law targets **conduct, not belief**.  
> â€“â€¯Terms are no vaguer than â€œobscenityâ€ or â€œclear and present danger,â€ and ample administrative review cures any marginal uncertainty.

> **Level of Scrutiny Applied**  
> â€“â€¯Effectively **strict scrutiny**: laws burden **core political speech** in a uniquely sensitive forum (higher education); state must show **narrowly tailored means to a compelling end**, which it fails.

> **Significanceâ€¯/â€¯Immediate Fallout**  
> â€“â€¯Landmark for **academic freedom**: First time the Court constitutionalized the concept and invalidated loyalty oaths on that basis.  
> â€“â€¯Overruled _Adler_; accelerated dismantling of **McCarthyâ€‘era teacher loyalty laws** nationwide.  
> â€“â€¯Foreshadowed later tilt against â€œguilt by associationâ€ (_Oâ€™Hair_, _Roberts_).  
> â€“â€¯Cited in countless facultyâ€‘speech cases and in modern debates over **campus ideological mandates**, showing Courtâ€™s skepticism toward stateâ€‘imposed intellectual conformity.

> **Socraticâ€‘Class Landminesâ€¯&â€¯Answers**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œWhy did the Court rely on vagueness rather than decide a broad â€˜academicâ€‘freedomâ€™ right?â€  
> â†’ **Brennan used vagueness/overbreadth as _narrowest grounds_, but embedded a robust academicâ€‘freedom principleâ€”making the holding both doctrinally cautious and normatively strong.**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œHow is this different from **security clearance** loyalty checks for nuclear scientists?â€  
> â†’ **Clearances review _specific conduct_ and are handled in camera; Feinberg banned even silent association and public classroom speech, reaching far broader.**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œDoes Keyishian mean states can never condition employment on association?â€  
> â†’ **Noâ€”under _Scales_, the state may act when it proves **knowing, active membership + specific intent to further unlawful ends**. Mere status is insufficient.**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œWould a statute targeting only **active advocacy of violent overthrow in class** survive?â€ 
> â†’ **Possiblyâ€”if narrowly drawn, viewpointâ€‘neutral, and keyed to direct incitement (_Brandenburg_) rather than abstract doctrine.**  
> â€“â€¯_Q:_ â€œWhat if a professor openly leads a militant group calling for insurrection?â€  
> â†’ **State can discipline based on **incitement / true threat** standards; Keyishian protects academic inquiry, not violent conspiracies.**

## Week 6 Office Hour (No Discussion)

### Legal Reasoning & Opinion Styles

- **Meyer** (used in 2-year travel ban argument)
    - Possibly a stretch in reasoning.
    - Example of a more **Sotomayor-style opinion** â€” emotionally grounded, rights-expansive.
- Difficulty in **summarizing opinions**:
    - Supreme Court language is dense and verbose.
    - Syllabus summaries are helpful but hard to craft succinctly.

### Marriage Rights as Legal History

- If researching **marriage as a legal right**:
    - Look at **case citation networks** in:
        - _Meyer v. Nebraska_
        - _Loving v. Virginia_
        - _Obergefell v. Hodges_
    - Question: Can a **right to divorce** be _invented_ analogously from _Obergefell_ or _Loving_?

### TikTok Ban & the First Amendment

- Not likely to be discussed in class:
    - Too **politically charged**
    - Involves **corporate law** & **executive deference**
    - Doesnâ€™t fit within **clean doctrinal lines** of First Amendment jurisprudence
    - Too many **overlapping First Amendment cases** to draw a singular principle

### ==Grisinger's Legal Career & Reflections==

#### Private Sector (BigLaw) ðŸ‘Ž

- **Summer associate life**:

        - Work-life balance â€œreally, really hardâ€

    - Most litigation = same cases for years, just cycles of paperwork
    - â€œThatâ€™s what the money is forâ€ â†’ but not worth the lost time

#### Legal Academia ðŸŽ‰ðŸ‘

- **Teaching & Research** as a professor:
    - More freedom than lawyers: **â€œnot bound by clients and partnersâ€**
    - **Almost absolute control over your time and syllabus**

        - Mandated syllabi = feel like a job, not a passion
    - Once taught many times, class planning becomes modular (â€œcan add a day, rearrangeâ€)
- **Preferred lifestyle:**
    - Self-paced, self-designed intellectual career
    - Less lucrative than BigLaw, but ==**â€œTIME is really a luxuryâ€**==
        - Willing to â€œtrade money for timeâ€
        - â€œLike a queenâ€ in the classroom â†’ absolute authority, flexibility, and rewarding
